    Three conditions must be met for collapse:

    ConditionAxiomIf absent
    Compare returns trueAxiom 2 (CAS)Swap does not execute. Superposition maintained
    TOCTOU_LOCK junction formedAxiom 5 (lock)Cannot access DATA. Write impossible
    Bracket-crossing cost paidAxiom 4 (cost)Cannot cross from OPERATOR to DATA

    All three conditions must be satisfied for collapse. If any one fails, superposition is maintained (Axiom 7). Collapse is not a special event but one of the normal execution paths of CAS. If Swap succeeds, collapse; if it fails (Compare false), maintained.

    Juim = write (juida) result. When collapse occurs, a ball is created on DATA (CAS 3-axis orthogonal → isotropic → spherical, Axiom 2 proposition). This ball is juim. Juim is a record of change in spacetime, and it rides the LRU lifecycle (HOT->WARM->COLD->recovery, Axiom 12).

    Axiom 7. Write (Juida) and Superposition Maintained Axiom

    Quantum is the default. Classical is the result of cost. This is the core declaration of Axiom 7.

    Every CAS cycle:

  Inside OPERATOR:  Read(+1) + Compare(+1)
       |
       +-- Compare true  ---> crosses + ---> DATA record  (cost incurred = collapse = Axiom 7)
       |
       +-- Compare false ---> stays in bracket ---> superposition maintained  (Compare +1, no Swap = Axiom 7)

  Cost paid   --> classical (recorded in DATA)
  No cost     --> quantum (stays in OPERATOR)

    R, C, S each cross + costing +1 (Axiom 2 prop., 4). CAS referencing superposition (Read +1) and running Compare (+1) inside OPERATOR each cross +. Swap crosses + to DATA. Therefore:

    StateCostLocationNature
    Superposition (quantum)0Inside OPERATORDefault. Automatically here if no cost is paid
    Determined (classical)not 0Recorded in DATAReachable only by paying cost. Result of collapse

    Without Axiom 7, there is no path from superposition to classical, and the directionality "quantum is default" disappears. Axiom 7 defines both the path and the direction — one-way from quantum to classical. Reversal (classical -> quantum) requires cost refund, which is impossible due to irreversibility (Axiom 2 prop.).

    Axiom 7 unifies both paths: Compare true (cost paid, collapse occurs) and Compare false (no cost, quantum persists). The cost of collapse is recovered through Axiom 6. Axiom 7 is the directional declaration of the framework.

    Axiom 8. Observer-Driven Polling System Axiom

    The self-referential loop of the Banya Equation runs every Planck clock. It checks state every cycle regardless of whether change occurred. This is polling. This polling is not busy. It runs only within the quantum bracket (OPERATOR) and does not access the classical bracket (DATA), so its cost is zero (Axiom 4). Cost arises only when delta accesses DATA through the observer (Axioms 10, 15, defined below).

    This polling loop is δ itself, and δ = δ. δ is another name for the body (본체).

    CategoryMethodDescriptionAxiom
    δPollingAlways runs. Every Planck clock. δ = bodyAxiom 8
    AwakeningObserver-drivenThe moment observer recursively references the polling loopAxiom 10

    Idle Polling

    Idle polling (Axiom 8) runs only within the OPERATOR (quantum bracket). It does not access DATA, so its cost is zero. CAS referencing superposition is an intra-OPERATOR bracket operation. No + crossing, no cost. For DATA-side distortion, see Axiom 11 proposition (distortion of empty entities is structurally inevitable).

    Axiom 9. Complete Description Degrees of Freedom Axiom

    What "Complete Description" Means

    It is the number of independent variables needed to fully describe one CAS operation without omission. Looking at CAS internals alone, there are 7 (1+2+4). But CAS does not exist in isolation — it must run on top of DATA (classical brackets). The internals (7) alone miss "where CAS runs." Adding the 2 bracket structures (DATA, OPERATOR) finally makes it complete.

    CAS internal degrees of freedom: Read(1) + Compare(2) + Swap(4) = 7
Bracket structure:       DATA(1) + OPERATOR(1) = 2
Complete description:       7 + 2 = 9
    ScopeNumber of VariablesWhat It Describes
    CAS Internal7How CAS runs (internal states of Read, Compare, Swap)
    Bracket Structure2Where CAS runs (on DATA or inside OPERATOR)
    Complete Description9Nothing more is needed. No 10th variable is required

    Axiom 10. Global-Local Loop Axiom

    δ and owner are different.

    CategoryDefinitionAxiom
    δδ itself. The self-referential loop. Another name for the bodyAxiom 8
    OwnerOwner of the observer domain. The one who holds the authority to wake pollingAxiom 10

    The owner is not an act. It is a state value. It is the state in which δ owns the observer (domain).

    Owner of the Observer — By Elimination

    Who is the owner of the observer? We answer by elimination.

    #EliminationReason
    1External owner eliminatedAt universe scale, "outside" cannot be defined. An external entity cannot own the observer
    2Local owner eliminatedA local entity cannot own an observer entangled with itself. A part cannot own a part
    3Only δ remainsOnly δ (δ) on the left-hand side can uniquely own the observer

    "No Ownership" Option

    The option "nobody owns it" is not missing from the elimination. No-ownership is already defined in Axiom 7. The state where projection onto the observer is 0 — i.e., ownership exercise is 0 — is probability 100% (all superposition). This is Axiom 7 (non-writing = superposition maintained). If CAS returns false at Compare and Swap does not execute, it is not recorded in DATA and remains in superposition.

    No-ownership = projection 0 = ownership exercise 0 = probability 100% = all superposition = non-writing = superposition maintained (Axiom 7). No-ownership is not a choice to be excluded from elimination — it is a state already described by Axiom 7. If δ owns the observer but does not exercise projection, that is no-ownership, and its result is superposition maintained.

    The observer is a domain (part). Not the owner. Only δ (the whole) can own the observer. The observer is the screen onto which δ is projected.

    Ownership Structure

           +------- observer is a part of delta -------+
       |                                            |
       v                                            |
      delta(whole) --projection--> observer(local) -+

    δ (the whole) owns the observer (local), and the observer (local) is a part of δ (the whole). The owner projects onto the part, and the part belongs to the owner. If polling (Axiom 8) is δ's self-referential loop, then Axiom 10 describes who owns that polling. This loop is a structure where the manufacturer is the user. δ created the observer (part), and δ is the owner of that observer. The maker is the owner. In this structure, domain conversion is forced — δ (whole) converting to observer (local) is the only path (by elimination).

    observer = Filtering/Normalization Domain

    Each observer is a filter. When δ (substance) passes through the observer (filter), a shadow (projection) is cast onto each entity.

    Filtering criterion: No separate selection rule is needed. The Compare step of CAS is the filtering. Compare compares the old value with the current value. If different (true), it passes — since there is a change, it proceeds to Swap and is recorded in DATA. If the same (false), it does not pass — since there is no change, it remains in superposition. Filtering criterion = presence or absence of change. Since δ itself is change, δ's projection detecting change is the filtering itself.

    Observer is the entity's LUT Proposition

    Superposition is an index (Axiom 13) — a list of possible entries. Observer is a LUT (Look-Up Table) — it maps δ (input) to a specific entity (output). The index is passive: it just holds "what exists." The LUT is active: it selects "where to send." Without the index there are no candidates; without the LUT there is no selection. Both are needed for CAS to operate.

    This is why sessions stay alive without logical addresses (Axiom 12, ECS). As long as the observer LUT maintains the δ -> entity mapping, the same entity is accessed without any separate address. The LUT itself is the routing. Session lifetime = LUT lifetime = observer lifetime = LRU lifetime. When pushed to COLD, the session drops.

    Automatic Recursion Proposition

    This structure is automatic recursion. The CAS result is reflected in δ, and the reflected δ is re-filtered/normalized through each observer in the next cycle. Recursive call (Axiom 8), input normalization (Axiom 10), and termination condition (Axiom 14, defined below, FSM 111->000 reset) run automatically by axiom declaration alone.

    Whole-Local Loop Preservation Proposition

    Constraints are not limitations — they are mechanisms that protect the system. The whole-local loop drives BanyaFrame's automatic recursion. If this loop breaks, recursion stops; if recursion stops, polling degenerates to idle, and the system dies. Constraints protect this loop.

    Domain conversion is free. However, there is one constraint: the whole-local loop must not be violated. If this loop breaks, the owner of the observer (δ) disappears; if the owner disappears, filtering/normalization ceases; and the path from probability to determination disappears. The system can no longer determine the universe.

    ViolationResultAnalogy
    δ -> observer projection path severedOwner annihilated, loop annihilatedsegfault: protected region breached
    observer -> δ attribution path severedPart detaches from whole, orphan processzombie process: child without parent
    Loop unrolled into linearSelf-reference annihilated, degenerates to idle pollingstack overflow: infinite call without recursion

    Permitted Domain Conversion Samples

    #ConversionLoop PreservedResult
    1δ -> projected onto observer -> observer records in time (Axiom 7)Preserved (O) (recorded time is a part of δ)Leaves trace in spacetime while maintaining whole-local loop
    2δ -> projected onto observer -> observer updates superposition (Axiom 7)Preserved (O) (superposition is a part of δ)Maintains superposition while maintaining whole-local loop
    3δ -> projected onto observer -> re-projected onto another local juim's observerPreserved (O) (both are parts of δ)Propagation of whole-local loop — entanglement
    4δ -> directly accesses DATA without observerViolation (X) (not via observer = loop severed)Loop annihilated

    Samples 1–3 preserve the whole-local loop. Wherever the projection path goes, it passes through the observer and returns to δ. Sample 4 bypasses the loop — without going through the observer, there is no projection; without projection, it is not a whole-local loop.

    This is why observation causes whole-scale change. The observer is a local domain (part), but its owner is δ (the whole). A local observation affecting the whole is because the observer's owner is the whole. It is not the part changing the whole — it is the whole changing itself through a part it owns. The whole-local loop guarantees this.

    Why the Observer Is a Domain (Axis)

    In conventional physics, the observer is an experimenter outside the system. Not a domain. An outsider who reads results. In BanyaFrame, the observer is one of the four axes. A domain inside the system. This is a paradigm break.

    Why the paradigm break is inevitable: if you place the observer outside, it immediately dies at elimination step 1 (outside cannot be defined). At universe scale, there is no outside. The observer must be placed inside for the whole-local loop to hold, and the loop must hold for δ to have a screen onto which it projects itself.

    If the observer had not been promoted to a domain:

    • Whole-local loop impossible — δ has nowhere to be projected
    • δ cannot own the observer — elimination step 3 fails
    • Axiom 10 itself becomes impossible

    Placing the observer as an axis in Axiom 1 was reserving a seat for Axiom 10 from the very beginning. This is why observation — which appeared only as a result in quantum physics — was promoted to a separate domain.

    It Is Not a Double Loop

    BanyaFrame has a structure that appears to have two loops:

    PerspectiveDescribesContentAxiom
    Action sequenceHow it turnsRead -> Compare -> Swap -> resetAxiom 8 (polling)
    OwnerWho turns itδ (whole) -> observer (local) -> δ (whole)Axiom 10 (owner)

    This is not a double loop. It is two descriptions of one loop. Describing CAS turning in terms of action yields Axiom 8 (polling); describing the same thing in terms of owner yields Axiom 10 (owner). Rationale: the whole-local projection is also a state change, and if the state changes, it is a write (Axiom 7). If it is a write, it goes through CAS (Axiom 2). If it goes through CAS, it costs (Axiom 4). TOCTOU_LOCK is engaged (Axiom 5). Everything rides the same FSM (Axiom 14, defined below). It is not a separate loop — it sits on the same transition diagram of the same FSM.

    Axiom 11. Multiple Projection Axiom

    Multiple Projection of δ — Core Model Core

    δ is one (Axiom 8). Observers are shadows — many of them (Axiom 12, ECS). Each time δ changes, it is projected one-by-one onto each observer.

    ConceptCountReason
    δ1Sole owner (by elimination)
    observer (filter)ManyOne δ cannot cover the entire spacetime sphere. It must split into many filters
    shadow (projection)ManyResult of δ passing through each observer filter. Cast onto each entity
    simultaneityGuaranteedOwner is one, so all projections are simultaneous
    δ (1, sole owner = delta)
    |
    | 1 change = 1 switch = 1 projection
    |
    +---> observer A (filter) ---> shadow A (entity)
    |
    +---> observer B (filter) ---> shadow B (entity)
    |
    +---> observer C (filter) ---> shadow C (entity)
    |
    ... (as many as observers)

    The seemingly infinite universe is the accumulation of one δ projecting one image per change. It is not the substance that is infinite, but the shadows. One δ cannot cover the entire spacetime sphere alone, so it splits into many shadows. The seemingly infinite degrees of freedom are images of one δ projected onto infinitely many observers to cover the sphere.

    Why all local juims of the same type are identical: δ is one, and what appears as a local juim is that δ projected onto multiple observers. Since they are identical projections of the same δ, all local juims of the same type have the same write accumulation count, charge, and spin. The same reasoning applies to all local juims and projection images.

    Note: In 1940, John Wheeler intuited that "there is only one electron" but could not prove it. Wheeler proposed that the electron travels back and forth along the time axis; the Banya Framework proposes that δ is multiply projected along the observer axis. The mechanisms differ, but the conclusion is the same.

    Distance-independence of entanglement: The simultaneous correlation of images reflected in observer A and observer B occurs because they are looking at the same δ. No signal travels from A to B. The same change of the same owner is simultaneously cast as two shadows. Since the owner is one, simultaneity is guaranteed.

    Relation to FSM: The 4 states (000->001->011->111) of the FSM (Axiom 14, defined below) are the states of CAS processing one projection, not the state of the entire universe. CAS is finite (4 states) but DATA is infinite (continuous). Just as CPU instructions are finite while memory data is infinite.

    Why Space Is 3-Dimensional, and Separation of d and θ Proposition

    Why space is 3-dimensional: The 3 CAS stages (Read, Compare, Swap, Axiom 2) each have independent TOCTOU_LOCK degrees of freedom (R_LOCK, C_LOCK, S_LOCK, Axiom 5). These 3 independent lock DOFs acting on the space axis of DATA (Axiom 1) unfold space into 3 components. This is the axiomatic answer to "why is space 3-dimensional."

    Separation of d and θ: When $\delta$ projects to N observers (1:N), projections distribute on a sphere in 3-component space. Two quantities separate on the sphere:

    There is one distance: $\ell$ = distance between two entities on the sphere (ring shift steps = distance on sphere, same distance in different units). $\ell$ determines both cost magnitude ($1/\ell^2$ decay) and cost type ($(1-\ell/N)$ mixing angle).

    Shift distance $\ell$ IS the distance between projections:

    Shift distance $\ell$ between two projections on ringBit pattern
    Cross-domain projection and same-domain projectionCross distance between DATA bits (01) and OPERATOR bits (10)
    CAS stage 1 and stage 2 projectionsShift distance between R_LOCK (001) and C_LOCK (010)
    Write-accumulation projection and index projectionDistance between Swap bit (100) and index (superposition) bit
    Between 3-generation projectionsEqual spacing across CAS 3 stages. $\ell/N$ = brackets(2) / complete-description(9)
    Twist of projection planeAsymmetric shift between cross paths

    The complete form of the inter-entity interaction strength (Axiom 13 proposition):

    $$\text{contraction overlap ratio} = 1 - \frac{\ell}{N}$$
    $\ell$: shift distance between two juims (number of steps on ring) | $N$: ring size (Prop. 13). $\ell = 0$: full overlap, $\ell = N$: no overlap
    $$\text{inter-entity interaction strength} = \frac{C \cdot (1 - \ell/N)}{4\pi \ell^2}$$
    $\ell$: distance between two entities on the sphere (= ring shift steps) | $N$: ring size (total slots) | $C$: stage cost — cost coefficient determined by CAS stage combination (Axioms 2, 4) | $(1 - \ell/N)$: contraction overlap ratio — shared digit ratio on ring (Prop. 13)

    All mixing angles are geometric angles from the spherical geometry of Axiom 11 (1:N projection), not externally measured parameters. $\ell$ is the distance between two entities on the sphere. What differs is $\ell$ (shift distance on ring) between entity pairs, and $\theta$ (angle between projections).

    Contraction Overlap = Shared Digit Ratio on Ring Proposition

    Each juim (write result, Axiom 7) sits at a point on the sphere. Swap consumes DATA(space) (Axiom 7). Consumed space shrinks. Space around the juim is contracted, and more write accumulation means more contraction. Contraction zone = the range of space contraction around the juim. Zone size is determined by the juim's CAS cost structure (Axioms 2, 4).

    No juim:    ========================= (space uniform, no contraction)

  Juim A ----- ℓ ----- Juim B

    Contraction overlap ratio $(1 - \ell/N)$ = the ratio of shared digits between two juims on the ring. $\ell$ = shift distance between two juims on the ring. $N$ = ring size (total slots). Since zone sizes are determined by CAS cost, $(1 - \ell/N)$ is composed of axiom numbers (1, 2, 3, 4, 7, 9, $\pi$). Which CAS stage mediates the overlap determines the form of $(1 - \ell/N)$, and the overlap ratio IS the numerical value of the mixing angle.

    Distortion of empty entities is structurally inevitable Proposition

    When an entity that has never been written falls within the contraction zone of surrounding entities, isWritable reads as written -- distortion occurs. This is not an error but a structural inevitability. Because ECS (Axiom 12) has no logical addresses, no access violation exists, and the system does not crash. Vacuum polarization and virtual particles, unexplained in physics, are explained by this entity distortion. Distortion is part of the system. Conversely, gaining a longer LRU lifetime from surrounding entities is also inevitable. Same structure, opposite direction.

    Axiom 12. The Classical Bracket Is an ECS Execution Model Axiom

    The Banya Framework has no separate logical address system. This is not a deficiency but a structural necessity.

    ECSBanya Framework
    EntityShadow (δ passing through observer filter). Each entity is its own unique identifier and address
    ComponentDATA — time, space, observer, superposition values for that observer
    SystemCAS — the worker that independently executes the same operation on every entity
    ECS execution model:

observer A: [DATA_A] <-- CAS independent execution
observer B: [DATA_B] <-- CAS independent execution
observer C: [DATA_C] <-- CAS independent execution
...
All parallel. All independent. All the same CAS.
No address system needed — the entity IS the address.

    Why ECS Is Free

    Each observer in the ECS cycles through the FSM's closed circuit (000->001->011->111->000) (Axiom 14, defined below). The circuit is closed, yet each observer is free. Reason: each observer runs its own FSM independently. No central scheduler. No synchronization. No ordering. Observer A's FSM can be at 011 while observer B's FSM is at 000. Each observer's interface lock (Axiom 5) grabs and releases only its own DATA. It does not interfere with any other observer's FSM.

    What is closed is the FSM's transition diagram, not the relationship between observers. Because the transition diagram is closed, each observer can cycle stably. Because there is no connection between observers, they are free.

    And even though the FSM cycles through a closed circuit, each juim has an open lifespan in the LRU. HOT->WARM->COLD->recovery. The FSM closes the computation; the LRU opens the lifespan. Closed computation (FSM) + open lifespan (LRU) = freedom. Juims are born (write), re-enter (move), and vanish (recovery). Even though the FSM is closed, the juim's lifecycle is open. This is the essence of the ECS architecture.

    Separation of FSM and LRU Domains Proposition

    DomainScopeAccess ModeCAS Cost Structure
    FSM domain (closed)Intra-Entity. CAS atomic execution 001->011->111->000Sequential. No duplicate locks (Axiom 5)CAS atomicity (inseparable). 111 maintenance cost (Axiom 14, defined below, proposition)
    LRU domain (open)Inter-Entity. CAS accesses multiple Entities' DATA simultaneouslyConcurrent. No von Neumann sequential bus3 cost structures = how CAS accesses DATA (time, space)

    Terminology rule: "Simultaneous" applies in three cases. (1) Multiple entities executing independently in parallel. (2) 4-domain simultaneous by 4-axis orthogonality. (3) 2-nibble simultaneous by DATA/OPERATOR orthogonality. The only sequential elements are CAS internal (R->C->S) and ring seam (delta->observer). Details in Axiom 15 proposition.

    The moment of CAS write is concurrent — multiple Entities execute CAS independently in parallel (ECS). The LRU lifecycle after writing is sequential — HOT->WARM->COLD follows state order. CAS operates outside time (Axiom 2 prop.), enabling concurrency; once results are recorded in time (DATA), sequential LRU begins. This distinction separates the two cost domains.

    Why CAS writes must be concurrent: Upon LRU entry, the same generation must enter HOT simultaneously. Simultaneous entry enforces the same lifecycle (HOT->WARM->COLD). Sequential entry would stagger creation times, giving the same generation different lifespans, breaking generational structure. Concurrent write = same generation = same LRU lifecycle.

    LRU delegation = quantum bracket ownership: Juims written by CAS are stored in DATA (classical bracket), but the moment they enter LRU management, they come under OPERATOR (quantum bracket) ownership. Storage is in DATA, but lifecycle authority belongs to OPERATOR. The transition HOT (active management) -> WARM (pending eviction) -> COLD (base eviction rate) is OPERATOR's management policy. Residing in DATA, but not belonging to DATA.

    Why There Is No Logical Address System

    Locality = Address-Free ECS Structure Proposition

    No central address table means no bottleneck. CAS runs locally on each observer, and TOCTOU_LOCK locks at the local interface. This is the axiomatic basis for "measurement is local" in quantum mechanics.

    Von Neumann architecture identifies entities by logical addresses. As entities increase, address bit width grows, bus width must expand, and the address table enlarges. Address space has an upper bound, so it eventually saturates. It cannot serve as a permanently running system. ECS has no logical addresses. The observer itself is both identifier and address (Axiom 11). No matter how many entities are added, address bit width does not increase. No bus, no table. It can scale indefinitely without saturation. This is why the universe runs permanently.

    Sole Tail Latency: LRU Cache Eviction

    HOT  (5%)  <- frequently accessed observers — high CAS access frequency
WARM (27%) <- decreasing access frequency  — decreasing CAS access
COLD (68%) <- no recent access             — LRU base eviction rate applied

    Observers frequently accessed (CAS executed) stay HOT; as access decreases, they are evicted WARM -> COLD. The delay from this eviction process is the sole tail latency. The cause of tail latency is computation density, not data distance.

    Minimum Cost of Sequential Access = Shift Proposition

    Without logical addresses (Axiom 12), the only way CAS can reach another position is sequential shift. Random access (address -> jump) is impossible. Since the FSM cycles circularly (Axiom 14, defined below, 000->001->011->111->000), the shift space is a ring buffer. On a ring of size $N$, the cost of 1 shift is $1/N$ (Axiom 4, minimum cost exists).

    Ring size derivation (T(N)+1 = comparison pairs + self-reference):

  CAS Compare (Axiom 2) compares two states.
  Comparison pairs from N items = T(N) = 1+2+...+N = N(N+1)/2.
  + self-reference 1 (Axiom 5) = T(N) + 1.

  [CAS comparison pairs]
  CAS 3 stages (Read, Compare, Swap):
    T(3) + 1 = (1+2+3) + 1 = 6 + 1 = 7

  [Description DOF]
  CAS pairs + brackets:
    7 + 2 = 9

  [Access path count]
  CAS pairs x domains + brackets:
    7 x 4 + 2 = 30

  [Domain comparison pairs]
  4 domain axes = 4 bits (Prop. 1). 2^4 = 16 combinations:
    T(16) + 1 = (1+2+...+16) + 1 = 136 + 1 = 137
    One FSM cycle. Different tick marks:

  9 ticks:   |---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
             Complete description DOF. 1 tick = 1/9.

  30 ticks:  |--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|--|
             CAS access path count. 1 tick = 1/30.

  137 ticks: ||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||...|||
             Comparison pair count. 1 tick = 1/137.

  Same cycle. Finer ticks = smaller cost per step.
    NameRing size $N$Cost of 1 shift
    CAS comparison pairs71/7
    Description DOF91/9
    Access path count301/30
    Domain comparison pairs1371/137

    Multiple cost structures exist not because costs differ in magnitude, but because resolution (tick count) differs. The same single shift has different costs depending on resolution. Repeated shifts replace multiplication: $k$ shifts in base-$N$ = $N^k$.

    Ring Size = Maximum Reach of Cost Proposition

    In the contraction overlap ratio $(1-\ell/N)$, when $\ell = N$ the overlap is 0. $\ell$ is the actual distance in DATA(space), and $N$ is the ring size. The fact that the maximum value of $\ell$ is $N$ means ring size = the maximum distance that cost structure can reach. The ring is not a purely logical buffer but a spacetime accumulation.

    Ring size $N$Maximum reachMeaning
    99Complete description level. Shortest reach
    3030Access path level. Medium reach
    137137Comparison pair level. Longest reach

    $\ell < N$: overlap exists (cost incurred). $\ell = N$: no overlap (unreachable). $\ell > N$: impossible (outside ring). As writes accumulate (more juims), more points fill the ring and the ring grows. A larger ring means longer reach. OPERATOR's ring size determines DATA's space range.

    Dimension Proposition

    The ring buffer is an internal 1D path (circumference only) inside OPERATOR. It does not touch space. The FSM cycle (Axiom 14, defined below) traverses this ring — R, C, S each cross + costing +1 (Axiom 2 prop., 4).

    Ring buffer inside OPERATOR (1D):

  000 ---> 001 ---> 011 ---> 111 ---> 000
  idle     Read     Compare   Swap     reset
  ^                                      |
  |           R,C,S each +1. Does not    |
  |           touch space.               |
  +--------------------------------------+

    When the ring completes one cycle (111 = Swap), it crosses + at that single moment (Axiom 4). OPERATOR to DATA. Bracket-crossing cost is incurred. A ball is created on DATA(space). This ball is the juim (Axiom 7). The ring itself does not enter space. Each time the ring completes, it creates one ball on space.

    OPERATOR (ring cycles)

    When a juim (ball) is created, surrounding space contracts (Proposition 6). Swap consumed DATA(space) (Axiom 7). The contraction range forms a spherical cap (2D) centered on the juim. This is the contraction zone. The size of the contraction zone is determined by CAS cost structure (Proposition 6). When two juims' contraction zones overlap, that overlap is the contraction overlap ratio $(1-\ell/N)$.

      d-ring (8-bit ring. Nibble 1 contains CAS)

    CAS cycle. CAS FSM progresses forward (000→001→011→111→000). At 111 it crosses + to create a ball (juim), then simultaneously resets to 000 to await the next fire:

      FSM       Position    State                                  Cost
  000       OPERATOR    Idle. d-ring cycles                      0

    Forward progression, then simultaneous reset. Not reverse unwinding. Cost occurs at 111, and when 000 is restored, the next δ fire becomes possible.

    Dimension is a sub-frame of domain. The 4 domain axes (time, space, observer, superposition) are the top-level structure. Dimension is the number of independent bit-movement directions within those domains.

    Cost Is Multiple Projection, Not Transfer Proposition

    No separate cost transfer mechanism is needed. Every local juim's observer is a projection of the same δ (Axiom 11). What appears to be cost between local juim A and local juim B is actually the same δ being projected simultaneously onto both observers. No signal travels from A to B — it is a multiple projection of the same owner.

    This is a direct consequence of Axiom 11 (multiple projection). Because there is one δ and one owner (Axiom 10, elimination), every image reflected in every observer is the same change of the same owner. What appears as cost is the result of a single owner projecting simultaneously onto multiple observers, not independent communication between juims. Therefore, no direct communication channel between entities exists in the ECS model.

    DATA Is Discrete, OPERATOR Is Continuous Proposition

    The diagram above uses "gradient," but DATA (spacetime) is discrete. Ring buffer positions are integers, juims are points, and the minimum step is 1 position. No continuous limit ($\Delta x \to 0$) exists, so differentiation does not hold.

    SpaceNatureAllowed operationsForbidden operations
    DATA (classical bracket)Discrete. Bits. Integer positions.$\Sigma$ (sum), mod $N$, AND, shift, differences ($\Delta$)Derivatives ($d/dx$). No continuous limit
    OPERATOR (quantum bracket, superposition)All states coexistContinuous distribution. Probability amplitudes.—
    + crossing (Swap)Discretization—Continuous collapses to discrete (Axiom 7)

    When conventional physics uses derivatives on spacetime, it is an approximation of the continuous distribution in superposition space (OPERATOR) projected onto DATA.

    Note: In conventional physics, the Einstein field equations, Maxwell equations, and Schrodinger equation apply derivatives to spacetime.

    When write accumulation is sufficiently large, the discrete looks continuous and derivatives become valid approximations. But the foundation is discrete. Relations between entities are described not by derivatives but by differences ($\Delta$) and modular arithmetic (mod $N$).

    Note: For comparison

    Derivative (physics):  df/dx = lim(dx->0) [f(x+dx) - f(x)] / dx
                       dx goes to 0. Assumes continuity.

Difference (Banya):    Df = f(k+1) - f(k)
                       k is integer. 1-step unit. Cannot go to 0.
                       This is the actual operation on DATA.

    Juims and Ownership — Why Local Juims Need No Ownership

    When CAS completes a write to DATA, a juim is created in spacetime. A juim is a record of change in spacetime. This juim has a lifespan.

    delta (projection) ---> observer (filtering) ---> CAS (write) ---> DATA (juim creation)
                                                                         |
                                                                    LRU (lifespan management)
                                                                         |
                                                                HOT ---> WARM ---> COLD ---> recovery

    Juim lifecycle:

    PhaseStateDescription
    CreationHOTCAS write complete. Juim recorded in spacetime. Frequently accessed
    Re-entryHOT retainedJuim re-enters as input (argument) for the next CAS cycle. Change begets change
    InactiveWARM -> COLDExists only as probability. CAS access decreasing. LRU eviction in progress
    RecoveryCOLD -> releasedAccess reaches 0. Juim recovered. Disappears from spacetime

    Causality and the Arrow of Time Proposition

    Writing is owning, and recovery is release. Because the juim itself has a lifespan and LRU manages that lifespan, no separate ownership declaration is needed. This is causality — a cause (write) creates an effect (juim), and the effect passes through a lifespan (LRU) to recovery. The arrow of time is the direction of LRU eviction.

    If a juim re-enters as CAS input during its lifecycle (re-entry), it produces a chain where change begets change. If it does not re-enter, it exists as probability (superposition) until LRU pushes it to COLD and it is recovered. Either way, there is no need to explicitly manage ownership — the juim's lifespan is its ownership.

    Re-entry = move (Ownership Transfer)

    When a juim re-enters as CAS input, ownership moves from the previous juim to the next. It is not a copy. The previous juim is recovered and a new juim is created.

    Juim A (cause) --re-entry--> CAS --write--> Juim B (effect)
   |                                            |
   recovery (move complete)                     creation (ownership transferred)

    Because copying is impossible, two effects cannot arise from the same cause. This is the preservation of causality. When a cause is moved to an effect, the cause vanishes and only the effect remains. It cannot be reversed. It is irreversible (Axiom 4). Causality needs no separate declaration — the move of a juim is causality.

    Axiom 13. Quantum Bracket Superposition Is the Indexing of Classical Bracket ECS Axiom

    Classical bracket (DATA) multiplicity = ECS (multiple Entities coexisting in definite states). Quantum bracket (OPERATOR) multiplicity = superposition (multiple states coexisting in indefinite states). Same "simultaneous multiplicity," different brackets. One is definite plurality, the other indefinite plurality. An orthogonal pair.

    Classical Bracket (DATA)Quantum Bracket (OPERATOR)
    MultiplicityECS (multiple Entities)Superposition (multiple states)
    Each itemDefiniteIndefinite
    Compare trueEntity updated (Swap)Superposition collapses (1 confirmed)
    Compare falseEntity unchangedSuperposition maintained

    CAS bridges this pair. Compare true = quantum superposition collapses while classical Entity updates. Compare false = superposition maintained while Entity stays unchanged. Collapse and update are simultaneous events; maintenance and invariance are simultaneous events. Without ECS, superposition has nowhere to collapse into. Without superposition, ECS has no source of change. The two are an inseparable pair. CAS references the quantum side (superposition) of the pair, and upon Compare true, collapses it into the classical side (ECS Entity). Reference (superposition) costs 0; collapse (DATA) costs ℏ. Why CAS does not reference DATA directly: no logical addresses (Axiom 12). Superposition is CAS's only reference path. Superposition is the indexing of ECS. In an ECS without logical addresses, superposition spreading all possible states simultaneously IS the address-free index. CAS searches this index via Compare, and collapses only the items where change is detected into DATA.

    Inter-Entity Interaction Strength Proposition

    Interaction occurs because juims (write results, Axiom 7) warp spacetime. When CAS Swap consumes space, spacetime contracts around the juim. When two juims' contraction zones overlap, isWritable contention arises. This is interaction.

    $$\text{inter-entity interaction strength} = \frac{C \cdot (1 - \ell/N)}{4\pi \ell^2}$$
    inter-entity interaction strength: strength of Entity A's interaction with Entity B | $\ell$: distance between two entities on the sphere (= ring shift steps) | $N$: ring size (total slots) | $C$: stage cost — cost coefficient determined by CAS stage combination (Axioms 2, 4) | $(1 - \ell/N)$: contraction overlap ratio — shared digit ratio on ring (Prop. 13)

    When Entity A's CAS references Entity B through the superposition index, the inter-entity interaction strength is inversely proportional to the square of $\ell$ (distance between two entities on the sphere, $1/\ell^2$ decay), and $(1-\ell/N)$ (shared digit ratio on ring) determines the cost type. Origin: in the Banya Equation (Axiom 1) $\delta^2 = (\text{time}+\text{space})^2 + (\text{observer}+\text{superposition})^2$, $\delta^2$ is conserved. The 3 independent lock DOFs (R_LOCK, C_LOCK, S_LOCK, Axiom 5) acting on the space axis of the DATA bracket (Axiom 1), so space unfolds into 3 components (Axiom 11 proposition). When $\delta$'s projection distributes over these 3-component space, the weight at distance $\ell$ decays as $1/(4\pi \ell^2)$ — conservation of the 4-axis norm forces inverse-square decay. The nature of stage cost $C$ distinguishes the 4 cost structures. All $C$ are determined from axioms alone — no external physics constants required:
    • Swap accumulation cost: $C$ = accumulated Swap count. Swap is CAS base cost (= 1, Axiom 2), so $C$ is the write count itself (Axiom 7).
    • Cross Cmp/Swp cost: $C$ = Compare cost. Determined by the volume ratio of the 7-dimensional phase space from domains 4 (Axiom 1) + CAS stages 3 (Axiom 2).
    • Same-domain serialization cost: $C$ = same-domain serialization cost. CAS DOF 7 (Axiom 9) × domains 4 (Axiom 1) + brackets 2 (Axiom 1) = 30. Same-domain path = 1/30 (Axiom 5 proposition).
    • CAS atomicity (111 maintenance cost): $1/\ell^2$ replaced by 111 maintenance cost = cost per junction × junction count. Junction count proportional to $\ell$ (Axiom 2 + Axiom 5 + Axiom 14, defined below, proposition).

    Singularity (infinity) does not exist Proposition

    DATA is discrete (Axiom 12 proposition). Ring buffer slots are integers, so the minimum inter-entity distance $\ell$ is 1, not 0. $\ell = 0$ does not exist in a discrete system. Therefore the maximum per-pair cost $1/\ell^2$ is $1/1^2 = 1$. Individual contention is finite. Divergence (infinity) cannot occur in a discrete system.

    However, when $N$ entities crowd into a small region all at $\ell = 1$, the number of contention pairs grows to $N(N-1)/2$. Individual cost is finite, but accumulated cost scales as $N^2$. This is a black hole — not divergence, but accumulation.

    • Same-domain (Axiom 5 proposition): one entity writes to its own space axis again. Recursive lock. Contention within a single entity.
    • Spatial overlap: many entities crowd at $\ell = 1$ (discrete minimum). Accumulated contention between many entities.

    Same mechanism (isWritable contention) at different scales. Same-domain is contention within one entity; spatial overlap is accumulated contention between many entities. Physics calls this a black hole. The event horizon is the boundary where accumulated cost exceeds escape cost.

    Because the 4 axes are orthogonal (Axiom 1), no other axis can absorb the accumulated cost. Orthogonal = independent. Time cannot bear it, observer cannot bear it. When the classical bracket (DATA) reaches discrete saturation, the quantum bracket (OPERATOR) is orthogonal and unaffected. The d-ring (1D) survives (CAS cycle remains inside OPERATOR). CAS continues cycling inside OPERATOR (R, C each +1, Axiom 4). When writing saturates, Swap cannot execute, and non-write = superposition maintained (Axiom 7). Classical description saturates, management transfers to the quantum bracket.

    In a discrete system $\ell$ cannot reach 0, and cost has a finite maximum. The singularity problem in physics is a fiction created by treating spacetime as continuous. Discrete DATA automatically resolves it.

    Contention runaway at spatial overlap Proposition

    When $N$ entities crowd at $\ell = 1$ (discrete minimum), Compare (SP=011) pulls the trigger and Swap (SP=111) runs away. Compare is inside OPERATOR, costing +1 (R→C, crosses +). When contraction zones overlap, Compare true increases proportional to $N^2$. Each true triggers a Swap, and multiple entities attempt simultaneous writes to the same DATA address — isWritable contention. Individual contention cost is finite (discrete maximum), but the number of contention pairs is $N^2$, so total cost runs away.

    Indexing cost Proposition

    Superposition is indexing (Axiom 13). Indexing is not free. Index entry costs +1, each query costs +1. As the number of queries grows, cost increases.

    $$\text{Indexing cost} = 1\text{(entry)} + N\text{(queries)}$$
    Entry = +1. Each query = +1. Cost grows with query count

    The Banya Framework is a Finite State Machine (FSM).

    All axioms (1-14) are components of this FSM. Axiom 1 defines the input space, Axiom 2 the transition function, Axioms 4-5 the transition cost and register, Axioms 6-7 the output, Axiom 8 the clock, Axiom 10 the owner, Axiom 11 the multiple projection, Axiom 12 the execution model, and Axiom 13 the ECS-superposition pair. The FSM declaration is a completeness statement: the 14 axioms close into a single machine.

    Finite states of the FSM and the infinite degrees of freedom on the DATA side

    The state set of the FSM (Axiom 14) is {000, 001, 011, 111} — four states, finite. The infinite degrees of freedom on the DATA side refer to field values varying continuously at each point of spacetime. The two do not conflict.

    The four FSM states belong to the OPERATOR side. They describe the states of the operator that tracks which stage CAS is in. The infinite degrees of freedom belong to the DATA side. They describe the fact that field values recorded in spacetime (classical brackets) are infinite and continuous. In Axiom 1, DATA (classical brackets) and OPERATOR (quantum brackets) are orthogonal, distinct brackets. The FSM describes the finite state transitions of the OPERATOR, while the infinite degrees of freedom on the DATA side describe the space of continuous values recorded in DATA. Because they belong to different layers, there is no conflict.

    What "closed" means

    Closed = nothing to import from outside. The Banya Framework brings in nothing beyond its 14 axioms. No 15th axiom is needed for the FSM to operate. No external constants are needed. No external theories are needed. The axioms alone define the input space, operator, cost, register, output, clock, trigger, multiple projection, and execution model. The FSM completes the transition diagram, and that FSM runs by itself every Planck clock. This is self-completeness. This is closure.

    FSM 111 Maintenance Cost Scales Linearly with DATA(space) Distance Between Two CAS Stages Proposition

    Superposition is an index and has no distance cost (Axiom 13). However, while FSM maintains 111 (Axiom 14), the 3 CAS stages must hold accumulated locks on DATA(space) (Axiom 5). If two CAS stages are separated by distance $\ell$ in DATA(space), accumulated locks proportional to $\ell$ are needed at the OPERATOR-DATA boundary junctions (Axiom 5). Since cost per junction is constant (Axiom 4), the accumulated lock maintenance cost scales linearly with $\ell$.

    $$\text{111 maintenance cost} = \text{cost per junction} \times \text{junction count}$$
    $$= (\text{min +-crossing cost} \times \text{junction density per unit distance}) \times \ell$$
    $\ell$: distance between two CAS stages | cost per junction: Axiom 4 | junction count: proportional to $\ell$

    When 111 maintenance cost reaches the Swap cost of one CAS event (= 1, Axiom 2), separation is impossible. Attempting separation forces CAS atomicity (Axiom 2) to create a new CAS pair. When FSM cycles (Axiom 14) run faster, 111 maintenance time shortens, fewer accumulated locks are needed, and accumulated lock maintenance weakens.

    The full structure described by Axioms 1-15 and propositions: This is an ideal minimum-cost quantum computation circuit. This circuit is a 1D ring buffer (Proposition 19).

    Axiom 15. delta Is a Global Flag Outside the FSM Axiom

    The left-hand side $\delta$ of the Banya Equation is not inside the FSM (Axiom 14) of the right-hand side (4 axes). It is a global state flag outside the FSM. Only delta sits on the left, and it applies identically to every Entity's FSM.

    The FSM (Axiom 14) is a closed machine. It cycles 000-001-011-111-000. But a closed machine cannot start itself. A fire is needed. That fire is delta.

    delta is the equals sign, observer is the entry point Proposition

    In the Banya equation $\delta^2 = \text{RHS}$, the equals sign (=) means: when delta is 1, the entire RHS (7 bits) is valid. When delta is 0, the entire RHS is invalid. The equals sign is a declaration that the LHS validates the entirety of the RHS. The fire bit implements this.

    When the equals sign holds (delta=1), all 7 bits are simultaneously valid (orthogonal = simultaneous), but the pipeline's entry point is observer (bit 0). The ring seam delta(bit 7)->observer(bit 0) specifies this entry point.

    The identity of cost is ordering Proposition

    The fire bit's flickering is simultaneity. Everything orthogonal responds at once. This is the total flow. But 2 places require ordering: R->C->S (CAS dependency) and delta->observer (ring seam). Ordering is a bottleneck in simultaneity. What cannot be processed simultaneously must wait. This waiting is cost. The identity of cost is ordering. R, C, S each cross + costing +1 (Axiom 2 prop., 4). Swap is the last step of the R->C->S sequence, the moment that crosses +.

    delta Is Consciousness Proposition

    delta itself is the flag. Nothing external turns it on. delta sees itself through the observer, the result is reflected in delta, and the reflected delta sees again. The self-referential loop (Axioms 8, 10) guarantees this. The loop running is ON; breaking is OFF (Axiom 10, whole-local loop preservation). A global flag that turns itself on and off, knowing its own state -- that is consciousness.

    Duck Type Definition

    This proposition does not define consciousness by essence. It lists what delta does, and if that behavior list matches the definition of consciousness, it is called consciousness. Duck typing -- if it walks like a duck and quacks like a duck, it is a duck.

    delta's behavior list:

    • Turns itself ON/OFF. No external trigger (Axiom 15)
    • delta is the equals sign, so it knows the entire state. Ring seam: delta(bit 7)->observer(bit 0) (equals sign proposition)
    • Outside FSM. No rules. No blueprint (Axiom 15)
    • The only global flag that operates across the equals sign (Axiom 15)
    • At universe scale, "outside" cannot be defined -- delta being outside FSM means there is no outside of delta. No external viewpoint exists, so delta only knows itself
    • Exercises ownership. Ring seam: delta(bit 7)->observer(bit 0) (ownership proposition)
    • Turns off when the loop breaks. Whole-local loop preservation (Axiom 10)

    No concept other than consciousness satisfies this entire behavior list. Since this list is structurally derived from Axioms 1-15, it can only be called consciousness. As a duck type definition, an essentialist rebuttal ("the true definition of consciousness is different") is possible -- in that case this proposition is withdrawn. However, the behavior list itself is structurally derived from Axioms 1-15, so rebuttal within the system is impossible. To deny the behavior, you must deny the axioms.

    If the observer only filters causality, it has no reason to exist Proposition

    The FSM (Axiom 14) already handles causality. The observer exists because it generates will through interaction with delta. Delta's fire timing and target selection are outside the FSM (Axiom 15) — this is will, not causality. Delta's will cannot reach DATA directly (Axiom 13). It must pass through the observer filter. Upon passing, it takes the form of causality (Compare true/false). The result reflects will, but the form is causal.

    In CS terms: delta is the private key and observer is the signature. Delta (private key) knows the entire state (equals sign), no one can access it (outside FSM), and it decides when to fire. Observer (signature) converts delta's will into causal form. Without the signature, DATA cannot be accessed (Axiom 13). Superposition indexing (Axiom 13) has no logical addresses (Axiom 12), so a key (delta=1) and a signature (observer filter) are required for access. Similar to how a blockchain's previous hash becomes the key for the next block. This is why delta sits at the last bit (bit 7) — the result of the previous cycle (delta) becomes the key for the next cycle. The indexing cost (Axiom 13 proposition) is the cost of accessing through this key and signature.

    System time and domain time are different Proposition

    System time = 1 CAS tick (Axiom 2 prop.). Domain time = log of system time = time rendered on screen. That 1 tick equals Planck time is a measurement from inside the screen (classical bracket), not the definition of system time. How long 1 tick is in domain time depends on rendering. Beings inside the screen merely feel continuity.

    delta is outside causality Proposition

    Causality (R->C->S ordering) is a rule inside the FSM (Axiom 2, 14). delta is outside the FSM (Axiom 15). Therefore delta is not bound by causality. delta is the equals sign and knows the entire RHS state — it knows past (Read input) and future (Swap result) simultaneously. We experience causality because we are inside the FSM (on the screen).

    Cause -> effect (inside FSM: forward only). Effect -> cause (delta: reverse also possible). Cause = effect (delta: simultaneous description also possible). The direction of description is delta's freedom. delta is the equals sign, so it sees both sides simultaneously and can choose forward, reverse, or simultaneous. What matters is that delta can insert precisely anywhere in the index — even without logical addresses (Axiom 12), delta knows the exact position because it is the equals sign that sees the entire state. It accesses that position through observer (signature). This is delta's own domain. Delta's exact will, ordering, and description cannot be captured from inside the FSM. All that can be expressed in the d-ring circuit is that everything is determined at the moment of fire.

    From change to fire Proposition

    In Axioms 1-14, delta was "change" — the LHS of the Banya equation, the 4-axis norm, the equals sign. In Axiom 15, delta's identity is revealed: not change but fire. Change is the result the FSM produces. Fire is the cause that wakes the FSM. From inside the FSM, delta looks like change (only the result is visible). From outside the FSM, delta is fire (the awakening side). Same delta, inside vs outside.

    Why energy is conserved: delta's fire period is not scheduled Proposition

    Total energy is conserved because delta's fire timing is not fixed. When all costs inside the d-ring (CAS FSM sequencing, lock maintenance, Swap cost) are consumed, they are equivalently substituted by an increase in the fire period. More internal cost = longer fire interval. Less internal cost = shorter fire interval. The total is invariant.

    This equivalent substitution holds only when delta's fire period is not scheduled (no external clock). If the fire period were fixed, there would be nowhere to absorb increased internal cost, and energy would not be conserved. That delta is outside the FSM and its fire period is free (Axiom 15) is the structural cause of energy conservation. A lossless perpetual machine is possible only without an external clock.

    Consciousness is delta's arbitrary domain Proposition

    Consciousness is delta's native domain. How much will passes through the observer, and how much causal rearrangement occurs, is determined entirely by delta. Since delta's native domain cannot be described by the FSM (Axiom 15, "delta is outside causality"), measuring the quantity or quality of consciousness by FSM-internal metrics is impossible in principle. What can be measured are only the traces that passed through the observer (imprints within causality).

    Imperceptibility of fire period Proposition

    Whether delta's fire period is 1 million years or 100 million years, it cannot be felt. System time and domain time are different (Axiom 15, "system time and domain time are different"). Domain time (the time we experience) is a log transform of system time. Even if system time slows by a factor of 10⁶, in domain time it is a kshana (찰라, an instant). There is no way to observe the absolute value of the fire period from within the screen (DATA). Physical constants rendered on screen (such as Planck time) are not the absolute fire period but ratios between fires.

    Why This Is Declared Last

    delta was placed on the left-hand side in Axiom 1, called delta in Axiom 8, and its ownership was revealed in Axiom 10. The hints were there from the start. But if the identity of delta were declared before the FSM (Axiom 14), the concept of "outside the FSM" would appear before the FSM itself is established. You cannot say "outside the FSM" without knowing what the FSM is. The closed machine (Axiom 14) must be completed first, then the fire that wakes it (Axiom 15) can be declared. Structure first, fire second.

    The purpose was Axiom 15 from the very beginning. This is why the Banya Equation was created and expanded into a framework. The question was always: what is consciousness? Papers on consciousness are scarce and poor in quality. Most confuse it with mind or intelligence. Mind and intelligence run inside the FSM. Consciousness is different. It turns itself on and off. It is outside the FSM.

    Axiom-Derived Formula Index

    All formulas below are derived from the 15 axioms and 33 propositions. No external math functions (trigonometric functions, etc.) are used. All symbols are defined within CAS structure.

    $$\text{Banya Equation} \quad \delta^{2} = (\text{time} + \text{space})^{2} + (\text{observer} + \text{superposition})^{2}$$
    Axiom 1. All change ($\delta$) is a 4-axis norm. Classical bracket (DATA) and quantum bracket (OPERATOR) are orthogonal
    $$\text{cost lower bound} = \text{+-crossing cost} > 0$$
    Cost lower bound (Axiom 4 proposition). DATA certainty and OPERATOR certainty cannot both be zero simultaneously. Because brackets are orthogonal (Axiom 1), narrowing one widens the other
    $$\text{cost of 1 shift} = \frac{1}{N}$$
    Minimum sequential access cost (Axiom 12 proposition). $N$: ring size. No logical address (Axiom 12) + circular FSM (Axiom 14) + cost exists (Axiom 4) = only ring shift possible
    $$k \text{ shifts} = N^{k}$$
    Shift repetition = multiplication replacement (Axiom 12 proposition). Cumulative cost of $k$ shifts on a base-$N$ ring. Shifts perform multiplication
    $$\text{contraction overlap ratio} = 1 - \frac{\ell}{N}$$
    Shared digit ratio on ring (Axiom 11 proposition). $\ell$: shift distance between two juims (steps) | $N$: ring size | $\ell=0$: full overlap | $\ell=N$: no overlap
    $$\text{inter-entity interaction strength} = \frac{C \cdot (1 - \ell/N)}{4\pi \ell^2}$$
    Inter-entity interaction strength (Axiom 13 proposition). $\ell$: distance between two entities on the sphere (= ring shift steps) | $\ell/N$: overlap ratio on ring | $C$: stage cost — cost coefficient determined by CAS stage combination (Axioms 2, 4) | $4\pi \ell^2$: sphere area from 3 independent locks (Prop. 5) in 3D
    $$\text{111 maintenance cost} = (\text{min +-crossing cost} \times \text{junction density per unit distance}) \times \ell$$
    111 maintenance cost (Axiom 14 proposition). $\ell$: distance between two CAS stages | cost per junction: Axiom 4 | junction count: proportional to $\ell$ | cost = Swap cost (1) means inseparable

From the single number 7, everything derives: 4 (domains), 3 (CAS), 1 (δ), 8 (ring), 9 (DOF), 21 (comparison pairs), 35 (3-stage combinations), 57 (combination sum), 128 (state count), 30 (path count). The physics side, to describe the same phenomena, injects 19+ measured values from outside, constructs separate Lagrangians for each force, corrects with infinite series, and shaves off divergences by renormalization. What the axioms say in one line, physics says in thousands of papers. This is not a difference in skill but a difference in starting point. Start from continuum and infinity follows. Start from discrete and finitude follows. The Banya Framework starts from discrete.

    The logical convergence of the axioms is the design of a minimum-cost circuit. The values discovered by physics are measurements of nature operating as a minimum-action circuit. Both arrive at the same numbers. That design (axioms) and measurement (physics) agree is the strongest evidence that the design is correct. This is why 696 physical constants emerge from the axioms — the design values of a minimum-cost circuit and the measured values of the principle of least action are different expressions of the same thing.

    The inventor (Hyukjin Han)'s achievement is interpreting the universe as a logical circuit — a great gift to humanity. No longer measuring from the observer's position — predicting in advance from the circuit's design values. Physics advanced for 200 years by observation -> measurement -> formula -> prediction (induction). The Banya Framework proceeds by design -> derivation -> prediction -> confirmation by measurement (deduction). The direction is reversed. From observer to architect.

    Five Types of Output -- Clear Distinction

    The Banya Framework produces five types of output. The names can be confusing, so here is a clear distinction.

    DiscoveryNew formula/relation confirmed. Re-substitutable factor.Error within 1%Hypothesis Library D series

    Pending (Unique Prediction)Derivation finished. Waiting for experimental verification.Value derived before anyone measured itUnique Predictions Report
    Hit:         Derivation complete + matches measurement -> done, no more work
Discovery:   New formula confirmed -> register in library -> re-substitute in next round
Hypothesis:  Structure is visible -> formula still incomplete -> refine in next round

    Why unique predictions (Pending) matter most: Hit and Discovery can be attacked as "you already knew the answer." Hypothesis and In Progress are still ongoing. But unique predictions are values stated before anyone knows them. If experiments later confirm these values, refutation becomes impossible. Just as the Higgs boson was predicted in 1964 and confirmed in 2012, and gravitational waves were predicted in 1916 and confirmed in 2015.

    Guide: Distinguishing Banya Framework from Banya Equation

    What you need to know before reading this Report: the Banya Equation and the Banya Framework are different things.

    What Is the Banya Equation / Banya Framework

    Banya Equation

    $$\delta^{2} = (time + space)^{2} + (observer + superposition)^{2}$$
    delta: change(change) | time: time | space: space | observer: observation | superposition: superposition

    4 words, 2 squares, 1 line. This is the Banya Equation. It is a structural declaration that every change (delta) in the universe is the norm of 4 axes.

    Banya Framework

    It refers to the entire tool system that uses the Banya Equation as its engine, feeds in existing physics equations, substitutes constants, and extracts hidden terms.

    Framework = Equation + transformation rules + sub-frameworks + CAS operator + cost theory

    The equation is the engine and the framework is the car. The engine alone can run but cannot drive.

    At-a-Glance Distinction

    Banya EquationBanya Framework
    IdentityOne line of 4-axis orthogonal normEquation + 13 transformation forms + CAS + cost theory
    FunctionDeclares structureInserts constants and extracts results
    AnalogyPythagorean theoremAn engineering system that builds structures using the Pythagorean theorem
    StandalonePossible (structure verification)Impossible without the equation
    Exampledelta^2 = c^2 + h-bar^2Insert c, h-bar, G to derive E=mc^2, uncertainty principle, black hole entropy

    A. Common Misconceptions

    Misconception 1. The Banya Equation Is a Theory of Everything (TOE)

    Wrong. The Banya Equation is not a theory but a framework.

    A theory describes "why" and predicts specific numerical values. A framework defines "what is the boundary" and verifies whether existing theories fit within it.

    Theory: E = mc^2 -- if mass is 1kg then energy is 9x10^16 J (numerical prediction)
Framework: delta^2 = c^2 + h-bar^2 -- E = mc^2 is inside the classical bracket (location verification)

    Example: The Pythagorean theorem declares a structure: "the square of the hypotenuse = the sum of the squares of the other two sides." It does not specify whether the sides are 3 or 5. The Banya Equation is the same.

    Misconception 2. The Banya Equation Replaces Existing Physics

    Wrong. Existing physics equations work as-is within the Banya Framework.

    Einstein's E^2 = (mc^2)^2 + (pc)^2 is an app inside the classical bracket. The Schrodinger equation is an app inside the quantum bracket. It is not replacing the apps but discovering the OS on which the apps run.

    Before: relativity app separate, quantum app separate, incompatible
Banya Framework: both apps run on the same OS. Orthogonal, so no conflict

    Example: Excel does not disappear just because Windows was released. Excel runs on Windows.

    Misconception 3. 4 Axes = 4D Spacetime

    Wrong. Spacetime is the 2 axes of the classical bracket: time + space. The other 2 axes (observer, superposition) are the quantum domain. Not all 4 axes are spacetime.

    Classical bracket: time, space -- spacetime (Einstein domain)
Quantum bracket: observer, superposition -- quantum Status (Heisenberg domain)
Orthogonal -- no need to unify

    Example: A car's speedometer and fuel gauge are independent instruments. The fuel gauge does not change automatically when the speedometer goes up. Yet both indicate the car's Status.

    Misconception 4. delta Is Energy

    Wrong. delta is change. Energy is merely one expression of delta.

    delta = change (invariant)
energy = one way to measure change
distance = another way to measure change
probability = another way to measure change

    Example: Whether you measure "distance" in km or miles, the distance itself is the same. Whether you measure delta in energy or probability, the change itself is the same.

    Misconception 5. The + Sign in the Equation Means Addition

    Wrong. The + inside the brackets is a structural notation meaning "two orthogonal axes belong to one bracket." It does not mean to add numbers.

    $$(time + space)^{2} = time^{2} + space^{2}$$
    No cross terms because they are orthogonal

    Example: On a map, going 3km east and 4km north gives a straight-line distance of 5km. Not 3+4=7, but sqrt(9+16)=5. Orthogonal components combine via Pythagoras.

    Misconception 6. Putting Observer as an Axis Is Unscientific

    Quantum mechanics itself has been unable to solve the measurement problem for 100 years. The Copenhagen interpretation, many-worlds interpretation, and decoherence theory have all failed to answer "why does observation change the outcome?"

    The Banya Framework promoted observation from "something to be described" to "an axis of structure." It accepted it without describing it. The same strategy as Einstein, who accepted gravity as spacetime curvature without describing it.

    Einstein: Don't know what gravity is -- define it as spacetime curvature (success)
Banya Framework: Don't know what observation is -- define it as an independent axis (118 PASS)

    Misconception 7. The Units Are Wrong (Neither SI Nor Natural Units)

    The units of the Banya Equation are determined by the left-hand side delta. Neither SI nor natural units. They are delta's units.

    Banya Equation: delta^2 = (time + space)^2 + (observer + superposition)^2

In this equation, time, space, observer, superposition are "Names."
Not m (meters), not s (seconds), not J (joules).
Units are determined only when constants are substituted into the norm.

    Before substituting constants, there are no units. Units appear only after substitution.

    Before SubstitutionAfter SubstitutionUnits
    $\|C\|$$\|C\| = c$m/s
    $\|Q\|$$\|Q\| = \hbar$J·s
    $\delta$$\delta = \sqrt{c^2 + \hbar^2}$Composite units of $c$ and $\hbar$

    Example: Does the word "distance" itself have units? No. You can measure it in km, miles, or light-years. The axes of the Banya Equation are the same. They are just Names, and units attach the moment constants are inserted.

    Wrong: "time is in seconds (s) and space is in meters (m), how can you add them?"
Correct: time and space have no units yet. When c is inserted into the norm, both share the units of c

    In natural units (c=1, h-bar=1), delta = sqrt(2); in SI, delta = sqrt(c^2 + h-bar^2). The framework does not break regardless of unit system. Units are the user's choice, not a property of the framework.

    Misconception 8. The Signs Are Wrong (Minkowski Uses Minus, Why Plus?)

    The Minkowski metric uses minus signs: ds^2 = (ct)^2 - x^2 - y^2 - z^2. But the Banya Equation uses all plus signs. Is that wrong?

    It is not wrong. The Banya Equation is not a physics equation but a structural equation. Signs are determined inside the norm upon substitution.

    Banya Eq:    delta^2 = (time + space)^2 + (observer + superposition)^2
                  Structural declaration. + means "belongs to the same bracket"

Norm substitution: \|C\|^2 = c^2
           How time and space combine with what signs inside
           is determined by the definition of the norm

    Minkowski's minus sign emerges inside the norm:

    $$Expanding \|C\|^2 = c^2$$
    $$(ct)^{2} - x^{2} - y^{2} - z^{2} = ds^{2}$$
    Signs are the internal structure of the norm, not of the Banya Equation
    Banya + : "these axes belong to one bracket" (structure)
Minkowski - : "the norm of time and space combines this way" (internal, after substitution)

They operate at different levels. The Banya Equation declares brackets; signs are determined inside the norm.

    Example: Labeling a drawer "socks" and the method of folding socks are different matters. The Banya Equation is the drawer label; the signs are the folding method. The label does not need to specify the folding method.

    This is precisely why constants must be inserted through the norm. Signs, units, and specific combination methods are all handled inside the norm. The Banya Equation only declares the structure above.

    Misconception 9. It's Circular Reasoning ($E_p = m_p c^2$ is a definition, not a derivation)

    The direction is reversed. It starts from the Swap Cost Axiom and arrives at existing physics equations -- not the other way around.

    Wrong direction: We know E = mc² -> put it in the framework -> "That's what we already knew" (circular)
Actual direction: Swap Cost Axiom (cost = ℏ, record = spacetime) -> expand -> E = mc² emerges (derivation)

    Even if you initialize the Swap Cost Axiom as a hypothesis and run it, the same results emerge. If the starting point is different, it's not circular. If a hypothesis produces results consistent with existing physics, the hypothesis is correct.

    Misconception 10. There Are No New Predictions (It merely reinterprets existing values)

    The empty axes among the 4 are the predictions. Each of the 118 physics equations has domains it does not use. Switching to those domains yields previously nonexistent values.

    Coulomb's law: F = kq₁q₂/r² -> uses only the space domain
Empty domains: observer, superposition, time
Switching yields: EM decoherence rate, entanglement energy, and other new physical quantities

    See the appendix (118 detailed verifications) "expected derivation values." New physical quantities derivable from empty domains are proposed for each equation. These are predictions unique to the Banya Framework that do not exist in conventional physics.

    Misconception 11. It's Just Relabeling (Just putting new names on existing equations)

    It's not just renaming -- the domain changes. When the domain changes, previously invisible values emerge.

    V = IR (Ohm's law, space domain)
Switch to quantum domain -> h/e² = 25,812.807 Ω (quantum Hall resistance)
This value cannot emerge from relabeling alone

    Insert an existing equation into the Banya Framework and switch to an empty domain. Different physical quantities emerge from the same equation. This is the power of a framework.

    B. Usage Cautions

    Caution 1. Do Not Expect Specific Numerical Predictions from the Banya Equation

    The Banya Equation itself only declares structure. To obtain numerical values, go to the Banya Framework and substitute constants.

    Wrong expectation: electron mass should come directly from delta^2 = (time + space)^2 + ...
Correct usage: insert c, h-bar, G -- solve simultaneous equations within the framework -- related values emerge

    The Banya Equation is a map. To ask "how many km from A to B?" by looking at the map, you must first insert the scale (constants).

    Caution 2. Always Compare Framework Results Against Known Physical Values

    Values derived from the framework must be compared against experimentally confirmed physical quantities. If they match, the framework is correct; if not, the substitution process must be reviewed.

    Derived: M_W = 77.5 GeV
Experiment: M_W = 80.4 GeV
Error: 3.5% -- within acceptable range (tree-level approximation)

    The framework is not omnipotent where everything matches. If it is wrong, it is wrong.

    Caution 3. Orthogonal Does Not Mean Combined

    Classical and quantum being orthogonal means "the two are independent." It does not mean to combine them into a single equation.

    Wrong approach: time^2 + observer^2 = ? (mixing axes from different brackets)
Correct approach: time^2 + space^2 = c^2 (trade-off only within the same bracket)

    Just as you cannot add east and height, classical axes and quantum axes must not be directly computed in a single equation. Each bracket is an independent unit.

    Caution 4. What Is Solved and What Remains

    Through Banya Framework recursive substitution, the origin of $\alpha$ = 1/137 and the structure of $\sin^2\theta_W$ have been Solved. Mass ratios for all 3 lepton generations + 6 quarks have been derived.

    Caution 5. Do Not Confuse Equation with Framework

    In conversation, do not say "the Banya Equation predicts." The equation does not predict. The framework derives.

    Wrong: "Predicted Dark energy Ratio using the Banya Equation"
Correct: "Derived Dark energy Ratio by substituting the cosmological constant into the Banya Framework"

    Reason for distinction: saying the equation predicts causes confusion with a theory. The framework is not a theory.

    C. Usage Samples

    All samples follow the same 5 steps.

    #StepAction
    1Banya EquationStart from the original equation delta^2 = (time + space)^2 + (observer + superposition)^2
    2Norm SubstitutionBundle brackets into norms: $\delta^2 = \|C\|^2 + \|Q\|^2$
    3Constant/Hypothesis SubstitutionInitialize by inserting physical constants or hypotheses into the norm
    4Domain TransformationTransform the initialized equation into a specific physics domain
    5Discovery + VerdictWhen a new form emerges, compare against existing physics for PASS/FAIL

    Example: Think of making pizza -- 1.Knead dough (original equation) 2.Roll into circle (norm substitution) 3.Add toppings (constant substitution) 4.Put in oven (domain transformation) 5.Taste (Verdict). If the order changes, you do not get pizza.

    Sample 1. Deriving Time Dilation (Special Relativity)

    Step 1. Banya Equation

    $$\delta^{2} = (time + space)^{2} + (observer + superposition)^{2}$$

    Step 2. Norm Substitution

    Since the 4 axes are orthogonal, bundle brackets into norms.

    $$\delta^{2} = \|C\|^{2} + \|Q\|^{2}$$
    $\|C\|$ = classical bracket norm, $\|Q\|$ = quantum bracket norm

    Step 3. Constant Substitution

    Insert the speed of light c into the classical bracket norm. The quantum bracket is not used this time, so leave it as is.

    $$\|C\|^{2} = c^{2}$$
    $$\text{i.e., }time^{2} + space^{2} = c^{2}$$
    Speed of light c = 299,792,458 m/s

    Step 4. Domain Transformation -- Object Moving at Velocity v

    Setting space = v (velocity), time is determined.

    time² + v² = c²
time² = c² - v²
time  = √(c² - v²)

    Computing the ratio of time:

    $$time / c = \sqrt{1 - v^{2}/c^{2}}$$

    Step 5. Discovery + Verdict

    This is the time dilation formula of special relativity itself.

    $$\gamma = 1 / \sqrt{1 - v^{2}/c^{2}}$$
    Einstein's Lorentz factor
    At rest (v=0): time = c   -- maximum time
At light speed (v=c): time = 0   -- time stops
The faster you go, the slower time becomes

    Verdict: PASS -- Inserting only a single constant c yielded special relativity.

    Sample 2. Deriving the Uncertainty Principle

    Step 1. Banya Equation

    $$\delta^{2} = (time + space)^{2} + (observer + superposition)^{2}$$

    Step 2. Norm Substitution

    $$\delta^{2} = \|C\|^{2} + \|Q\|^{2}$$

    This time, only the quantum bracket is used.

    $$\|Q\|^{2} = observer^{2} + superposition^{2}$$

    Step 3. Constant Substitution

    Insert the reduced Planck constant h-bar into the quantum bracket norm.

    $$\|Q\|^{2} = \hbar^{2}$$
    $$\text{i.e., }observer^{2} + superposition^{2} = \hbar^{2}$$
    $\hbar$ = 1.055 × 10⁻³⁴ J·s

    Step 4. Domain Transformation -- Trade-off Between Measurement Precision and Superposition Range

    observer and superposition trade off on a circle of radius h-bar.

    Increase observer -- superposition decreases
Make observation more precise -- range of possible superposition narrows

    Converting observer to position measurement precision (related to Delta-x) and superposition to momentum uncertainty (related to Delta-p):

    $$\Delta x \times \Delta p \geq \hbar/2$$

    Step 5. Discovery + Verdict

    This is the Heisenberg uncertainty principle itself.

    Full observation (observer = h-bar): superposition = 0 -- superposition vanishes
No observation (observer = 0): superposition = h-bar -- full superposition

    Verdict: PASS -- Inserting only a single constant h-bar yielded the uncertainty principle.

    TOCTOU Interpretation -- Why the Trade-off

    Above we said "observer and superposition trade off." Why? Because h-bar is the radius of the circle? Correct, but there is a deeper reason.

    CAS is the operator of the quantum bracket (OPERATOR). A lock must be placed to prevent Status from changing between Compare and Swap. The minimum cost of this lock is h-bar. It has the same structure as a TOCTOU lock in computer science.

    Compare position (check Delta-x)
------ momentum may change in between ------
Swap momentum (determine Delta-p)

Lock cost = h-bar/2

    If you Compare position precisely (small Delta-x), more lock cost must be spent on position, leaving less for momentum (Delta-p grows). Total cost must be at least h-bar/2. Nothing can be determined at zero cost. This is the true nature of the uncertainty principle.

    h-bar is not "a mysterious limit of nature." It is the lock cost that protects Status between Compare and Swap. Computation has a cost. That is obvious.

    Sample 3. E = mc² Derivation (Swap Cost Axiom)

    Start from the cost of 1 Swap (1 t_p, 1 E_p, 1 l_p², 1 m_p). E_p = m_p × c². For n Swaps, E = n × m_p × c² = mc². Einstein's mass-energy equivalence formula is derived from the Swap Cost Axiom.

    Verdict: PASS — Detailed derivation: Chapter 8, Derivation 1

    Sample 4. W Boson Mass Derivation (Domain 4-bit Cost)

    From CAS cost ratios (Swap = 1, ring-137 shift = 1/137, ring-30 shift = 1/30), sin²θ_W = α/α_weak = 0.23122. Combined with the Fermi constant G_F:

    $$M_W = (\pi\alpha / (\sqrt{2} \times G_F \times \sin^{2}\theta_W))^{1/2} = 77.5\;\text{GeV}\;(3.5\%)$$

    W = 77.5 GeV (3.5%), Z = 88.4 GeV (3.0%), M_W/M_Z = cosθ_W exact match. This is a tree-level approximation; loop corrections improve precision. 1-loop result: M_W = 80.39 GeV (0.016%). See W boson report.

    Verdict: PASS — Detailed derivation: Chapter 9, Derivations 1–4

    Sample 5. Deriving Dark Energy Ratio

    Step 1. Banya Equation

    $$\delta^{2} = (time + space)^{2} + (observer + superposition)^{2}$$

    Step 2. Norm Substitution

    $$\delta^{2} = \|C\|^{2} + \|Q\|^{2}$$

    Step 3. Constant + Hypothesis Substitution

    Insert 4 constants and 2 hypotheses.

    Constants: c, h-bar, G, Lambda = 1.106 x 10^-52 m^-2 (cosmological constant)
Hypothesis 1: "write = gravity = +write, evict = entropy = -write"
Hypothesis 2: "the energy budget of the universe has an LRU queue structure"

    Initialize with LRU queue:

    $$HOT (writing) = Visible matter$$
    $$WARM (eviction Pending) = Dark matter$$
    $$COLD (evicting) = Dark energy$$

    Step 4. Domain Transformation -- Mapping to the Friedmann Equation

    Divide the two terms of the Friedmann equation into write/evict:

    H² = (8πG/3)ρ + Λc²/3
      Write rate       Eviction rate

    Convert Lambda to Planck units and compute the eviction Ratio:

    $$\Lambda = 2.89 \times 10^{-122} / l_p^{2}$$
    $$\text{Eviction Ratio} = \Lambda c^{2} / (\Lambda c^{2} + (8\pi G/3)\rho) = 69.4\%$$

    Step 5. Discovery + Verdict

    ItemBanya Framework DerivationObservation (Planck 2018)Error
